## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, with state variables x (position) and v (velocity) evolving in time t, which is the standard phase-space form of an oscillator ODE: x' = v, v' = f(x, v, t). Nonlinear harmonic oscillators commonly include nonlinear restoring forces, damping (linear or nonlinear), and possibly external/parametric forcing depending explicitly on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = c0 * x (restoring acceleration proportional to displacement; sign encoded in c0)
- Linear damping oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (restoring plus viscous damping/anti-damping depending on sign of c1)
- Time-dependent stiffness (parametric oscillator): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric excitation with damping)
- Driven linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing added to linear dynamics)
- Pendulum (nonlinear restoring): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (small-angle reduces to linear; sin captures geometric nonlinearity)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring via cubic term)
- Higher-order polynomial stiffness: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (captures stronger nonlinear restoring at large |x|)
- Nonlinear (cubic) damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (aerodynamic/velocity-dependent damping nonlinearity)
- Van der Pol oscillator (state-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v (self-excited oscillations; damping changes sign with amplitude)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * v**2) * v (nonlinear damping leading to limit cycles)
- Liénard-type form (general nonlinear oscillator): dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * x + c3 * x**2) * v + c4 * x**3 (broad class combining nonlinear stiffness and damping)
- Conservative potential-gradient form: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * x)) + c4 * v (mix of polynomial and sinusoidal potential with linear damping)
- Nonlinear forced Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (canonical nonlinear driven oscillator)
- Parametrically driven Duffing: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * x**3 + c4 * v (nonlinear stiffness plus parametric modulation)
- Sign/absolute-value dissipation (dry friction / piecewise drag): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * Abs(v) * v (quadratic drag via Abs(v)*v; or approximates nonsmooth dissipation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative (energy-preserving) oscillator structure: dv_dt depends only on x (dv_dt = f(x)) and is typically odd in x for symmetric potentials; absence of v terms suggests no dissipation.
- Dissipation signatures: terms proportional to v, v**3, or Abs(v)*v typically oppose motion (coefficients with sign opposite v) and reduce amplitude over time.
- Self-excited/limit-cycle behavior: state-dependent damping such as (c0 + c1 * x**2) * v or (c0 + c1 * v**2) * v can create negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness: positive vs negative coefficients on x**3 (or higher odd powers) change how oscillation frequency varies with amplitude.
- Geometric nonlinearity / bounded restoring force: sin(c * x) implies periodic restoring (pendulum-like) and prevents unbounded growth of force with x compared to polynomials.
- External drive detection: explicit periodic functions of t (cos(c*t), sin(c*t)) in dv_dt indicate forced oscillations and resonance phenomena.
- Parametric excitation detection: time-varying coefficient multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t)) * x) indicates Mathieu-type instability bands and parametric resonance.
- Symmetry clues: if dv_dt is odd in x and odd in v (with appropriate signs), the system often has symmetric phase portraits; even-power terms (x**2, v**2) typically break odd symmetry via amplitude-dependent effects.
- Large-amplitude regularization: inclusion of higher odd powers (x**5, x**7) often models stiffening at large |x| and can prevent runaway solutions in fitted models.

Best expression     : c0*x**2 + c1*x + c2 + c3*exp(c4*t) + c5*v + c6*v*x + c7*v*x**2
Structure desc      : Quadratic polynomial in x plus exponential-in-t, augmented by a full quadratic-in-x polynomial scaled by v (v, v x, v x^2). With c5=0.600, c6=-0.910, c7=0.340, v strongly modulates both slope and curvature in x, while the base polynomial is 0.0878 x^2 -1.210 x + 1.325; t contributes a small decaying offset -0.202*exp(-1.875 t). The v-dependent part is not degenerate and can dominate changes across conditions. Approximate form: y ≈ (0.0878+0.340v)x^2 + (-1.210-0.910v)x + (1.325+0.600v) - 0.202 e^{-1.88 t}.
Fitted params       : c0=8.7816e-02, c1=-1.2102e+00, c2=1.3252e+00, c3=-2.0234e-01, c4=-1.8752e+00, c5=5.9951e-01, c6=-9.1003e-01, c7=3.4008e-01
Train NMSE          : 3.13e-06
Test NMSE           : 3.28e-06
OOD Test NMSE       : 9.66e-06

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (PO42)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*sin(x)*v - c1*beta*v
Candidate formulas: 119

GT (fixed):  
\[
-0.0313132230839372\,v^3\;-\;0.657729448450456\,v\sin(x)\;-\;1.31545889690091\,v\;+\;0.383670562566156\,\sin(t)
\]
So GT **must** contain simultaneously:
- a \(v^3\) term,
- a \(v\sin(x)\) coupling term,
- a linear \(v\) term,
- a pure \(\sin(t)\) term,
and **no** other \(x\)-only polynomials, exponentials in \(t\), denominators, logs, abs, etc.

Below, each candidate is checked for whether its available building blocks can be tuned (by choosing its constants) to produce exactly those four structures and nothing else.

---

### 1. \(c0 x^2 + c1 x + c2 + c3 e^{c4 t} + c5 v + c6 v x + c7 v x^2\)
Has only polynomial-in-\(x\) terms, \(e^{c4 t}\) (not \(\sin t\)), linear \(v\), and \(v x, v x^2\) (not \(v\sin x\)), and no \(v^3\). Cannot match.

### 2. \(c0 x^2 + c1 x + c2 + c3 e^{c4 t} + c5 v + c6 v x^2\)
No \(\sin(t)\), no \(v^3\), no \(v\sin(x)\). Cannot.

### 3. \(c0 x^2 + c1 x + c2 + c3 e^{c4 t} + c5 x^3 + c6 \cos(c7 t)\)
Has \(\cos(c7 t)\) which can become \(\sin(t)\) via phase only if it were \(\cos(t+\phi)\), but there is **no phase parameter** inside cosine (only frequency \(c7\)). \(\cos(c7 t)\) cannot equal \(\sin(t)\) for all \(t\) by choosing constants (since \(\sin(t)=\cos(t-\pi/2)\) needs a shift). Also no \(v\) terms at all. Cannot.

### 4. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 + c3 v + c4 e^{c5\sin(c6 x + c7 t + c8)}\)
No \(v^3\), no \(v\sin(x)\), and exponential-of-sine cannot be reduced to \(\sin(t)\) exactly for all \(x,t\) by constants. Cannot.

### 5. \( \dots + c5 \log(c6|v|+1)\sin(c7 t + c8)\)
Has \(|v|\) and log, not present in GT; also no \(v^3\) nor \(v\sin(x)\). Cannot.

### 6. \( \dots + c5 v^{c6} x^{c7}\)
Could make \(v^3\) by \(c6=3\), but then it is multiplied by \(x^{c7}\). Setting \(c7=0\) gives \(v^3\) term, but still no \(v\sin(x)\) and no \(\sin(t)\) (only \(e^{c4 t}\)). Cannot.

### 7. \( \dots + c5 \cos(c6 t)\)
Same issue as (3): cosine has no phase shift parameter; cannot become \(\sin(t)\) for all \(t\). Also no \(v\) terms. Cannot.

### 8. \( \dots + c5 x (c6+v)^{c7}\)
No \(\sin(t)\), no \(v\sin(x)\). Also introduces \(x\) factor. Cannot.

### 9. \( \dots + c6 x\cos(c7 t)\)
No \(v\) terms; also \(x\cos(\cdot)\) not in GT. Cannot.

### 10. \( \dots + c5 v|v|\)
Uses absolute value; GT has \(v^3\) (odd power) not \(v|v|\) (which equals \(v^2\operatorname{sign}(v)\)). Not globally equal. Also missing \(\sin(t)\) and \(v\sin(x)\). Cannot.

Has singular \(1/x^5\), not in GT; no \(v\) terms. Cannot.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO42)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*sin(x)*v - c1*beta*v
Candidates evaluated: 119
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: -0.0313*v³ - 0.6577*v*sin(x) - 1.3155*v + 0.3837*sin(t)**

The GT depends on: v, sin(x), sin(t), and v³. Let me analyze the key structural features:
- Terms involving v (linear and cubic)
- v*sin(x) term
- sin(t) term
- No polynomial terms in x or t alone
- No exponential terms

Let me check each candidate systematically. Most candidates have polynomial terms in x (like c0*x², c1*x) and exp(c4*t) terms. These cannot be zeroed out to match the GT unless we set their coefficients to 0, but then we'd lose the ability to represent sin(t) and v*sin(x).

**Key observation:** The GT requires sin(t), sin(x), v*sin(x), v, and v³. Any candidate that lacks these basis functions (and can't produce them) will fail.

Let me focus on candidates that have sin terms and v terms:

**Candidate 119:** c0*sin(c1*x + c2) + c3*x/(c4*t + c5) + c6/(c4*t + c5) + c7*v + c8*v³

This has sin(c1*x+c2), v, v³, and x/(c4*t+c5) + c6/(c4*t+c5). The rational terms in t cannot produce sin(t). Also, there's no v*sin(x) term. The sin term doesn't multiply v. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 83:** c0*sin(c1*x+c2) + c3*x/(c4*t+c5) + c6/(c4*t+c5) + c7*v + c8*v*x + c9*v*x²

Has v*x but not v*sin(x). The x/(c4*t+c5) can't produce sin(t). **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 25:** c0*x² + c1*x + c2 + c3*exp(c4*t) + c5*v + c6*v³

Set c0=c1=c2=0. Then c3*exp(c4*t) + c5*v + c6*v³. This gives exp(c4*t) but GT needs sin(t), and there's no v*sin(x) term. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 93:** c0*sin(c1*x+c2) + c3*x/(c4*t+c5) + c6/(c4*t+c5) + c7*v³

Has v³ and sin but no v*sin(x) coupling and no sin(t). **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 116:** c0*x + c1 + c2*x/(c3*t+c4) + c5/(c3*t+c4) + c6*v + c7*v³

No sin(x), no sin(t). **NO MATCH.**

Going through all candidates systematically, I need: sin(t), v*sin(x), v, v³. None of the candidates have the product v*sin(x) as a basis function, and none can generate sin(t) from exp or rational functions.

Let me verify there's no clever way to get v*sin(x) from any candidate... Looking through all 119 candidates, none contain a term like v*sin(x) or v*f(x) where f(x) could be sin(x).

Candidate 88 has v*(c8+x)^c9 - this is v*power(x), not v*sin(x). **NO MATCH.**

After careful review of all 119 candidates, none contain the necessary combination of sin(t), v*sin(x), v, and v³ basis functions required by the GT.
